  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cfc0f49c-b647-43a7-9eb9-826c1362ae92'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer8160050452628483166">For Tracey Rooks, life with her grandparents on a Wyoming farm has always been simple. But after her grandmother's death, Tracey is all her grandfather has. So when Eagle Elite University announces its annual scholarship lottery, Tracey jumps at the opportunity to secure their future and enters. She isn't expecting much-but then she wins. And life as she knows it will neve</span>
  <span id="freeText8160050452628483166" style="display:none">For Tracey Rooks, life with her grandparents on a Wyoming farm has always been simple. But after her grandmother's death, Tracey is all her grandfather has. So when Eagle Elite University announces its annual scholarship lottery, Tracey jumps at the opportunity to secure their future and enters. She isn't expecting much-but then she wins. And life as she knows it will never be same . . .<br /><br />The students at Eagle Elite are unlike any she's ever met . . . and they refuse to make things easy for her. There's Nixon, gorgeous, irresistible, and leader of a group that everyone fears: The Elect. Their rules are simple. 1. Do not touch The Elect. 2. Do not look at The Elect. 3. Do not speak to The Elect. No matter how hard she tries to stay away, The Elect are always around her and it isn't long until she finds out the reason why they keep their friends close and their enemies even closer. She just didn't realize she was the enemy -- until it was too late. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_666154218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666154218" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/666154218?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781455554164" href="/book/show/18170509-elite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666154218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11769338961859441751">I really didn’t care or connect to this story at ALL. I finished the book so I can firmly stand by my rating. <br/><br/>This story was a HOT MESS. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412944ra/812415.gif' width='400' height='310' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>The school Elite is completely <b>BIZARE</b> and not in a good way…more like in a completely unbelievable way. The children who attend are the superrich, the fabulously famous and mafia offspring. Our main character, Trace wins a scholarship to attend. She is a farm girl raised since the age of six by her grandparents, and oh yeah she loves COWS.<br/><br/> <br/>Nixon is the head of </span>
  <span id="freeText11769338961859441751" style="display:none">I really didn’t care or connect to this story at ALL. I finished the book so I can firmly stand by my rating. <br><br>This story was a HOT MESS. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412944ra/812415.gif" width="400" height="310" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The school Elite is completely <b>BIZARE</b> and not in a good way…more like in a completely unbelievable way. The children who attend are the superrich, the fabulously famous and mafia offspring. Our main character, Trace wins a scholarship to attend. She is a farm girl raised since the age of six by her grandparents, and oh yeah she loves COWS.<br><br> <br>Nixon is the head of the bully group, the president of the student body and his family owns the school. Nixon graduated but runs his deceased father’s numerous corporations and plays a “Lord of the Flies” kinda shithead at the school along with his three pals…The Elect. They keep order…lunch schedules, elevator passes while physically and emotionally tormenting the students to keep peace. Nixon's henchmen are Phoenix, an ass, and Chase, a sweetheart. <br><br><br>Anyway, farm girl Trace is immediately welcomed by the three otherwise known as The Elite with horrible words and insults. Trace endures hell at this school, she is branded a slut, drugged, bullied, egged, etc., never once does the thought cross her mind to LEAVE!!! <br><br><br>Trace stands up for herself. Nixon and crew treat her like crap. Nixon puts together who Trace is by a necklace which has a name on it. Not from recognizing her grandfather???? Big reveal <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her family is mafia as well! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Her grandfather put her in school so she could find out the truth of who she is (Not from him but from strangers) and to lure bad guys to make a play like bait..WTF?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428970ra/858914.gif" width="400" height="310" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Anyway, further reveal is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Trace is the LOVE of Nixon’s life because when he was 9 and she was 6 they had a forever bond and love <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Again…WTF?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428970ra/858915.gif" width="400" height="310" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I can honestly say that the only character that I liked was Chase. The story just didn’t work for me at ALL and I won’t be returning to Elite. <br><br>I’d much rather hang out with the cows! MOO!<br><br><i>*Arc provided by Net Galley via Forever (Grand Central Publishing)*</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11769338961859441751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/664820538?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer664820538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9759807491893648247"><b>I can't read this book any more... please don't make me. My brain hurts from reading just 24%... hurts so much...</b><br/><br/>I honestly thought that this was a joke book. A mockumentary if you will. It made no sense from the get go, and the dialogue was something maybe a five year old would write. <br/><br/>I'll give you a brief rundown of the plot before I purge this book from my memory. A country girl (Trace) wins a national lottery to go to an elite private school where celebrities and dignitary kids are enrolled.</span>
  <span id="freeText9759807491893648247" style="display:none"><b>I can't read this book any more... please don't make me. My brain hurts from reading just 24%... hurts so much...</b><br><br>I honestly thought that this was a joke book. A mockumentary if you will. It made no sense from the get go, and the dialogue was something maybe a five year old would write. <br><br>I'll give you a brief rundown of the plot before I purge this book from my memory. A country girl (Trace) wins a national lottery to go to an elite private school where celebrities and dignitary kids are enrolled. For some reason that makes absolutely no sense, as soon as she gets to campus she is mocked and greeted with hostility the likes of I have never witnessed in real life. <br><br><i>"We are untouchable. If you as much as sneeze in our direction, if you as much breathe the same air in my atmosphere, I will make our life hell."</i><br><br>Dude. Dramatic much??<br><br>The big bad mean boys don't just stop there. Apparently they also have access to Trace's key card to get her into all of the rooms and elevators on campus. They tell her that they are going to limit her food and freedom... just because... (what???). Does Trace get mad or ask them what crawled up their butts? No. She just cowers and pities herself and doesn't even consider getting out of this hellhole! However, of course, the head meanie (Nixon) is also apparently smoking hot and irresistible to our hapless heroine. <br><br><i>His eyes were a crystal blue, like the fires of hell had frozen over and the ice staring back at me was the result of orange flames dying slowly.</i><br><br>What. The. F. I tried to read that sentence three times before I gave up. <br><br><i>His entire face was symmetrically perfect. As if some famous supermodel and actor decided they should create a love child and programmed perfection in a computer.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428779ra/858245.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't even want to guess what the book is actually about. I don't care. I just can't believe I read another 20% after that point. I deserve a medal. <br><br>**Copy provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review**</span>

<div id="review_668861545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/668861545" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/668861545?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=insta-love-add-water">insta-love-add-water</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=wtf-concepts">wtf-concepts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment">bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=possible-creepers">possible-creepers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer668861545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17445407210812302128"><b>Welcome to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1087204.Ouran_High_School_Host_Club_Vol_01?ac=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ouran High School</a>!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355408ra/9791557.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>A school for the children of the richest and most influential families in <s>Japan</s> America. One day, a poor <s>scholarship kid</s> contest winner will stumble across the <s>Host Club</s> Elect, a gang of gorgeous, influential and money-laden bastards, who then take her under their wing!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355408ra/9791558.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Aft—what? *listens to earpiece* Oh, I'm sorry, I got it wrong. This isn't Ouran High School, it is, in fact, <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/832225.Eyeshield_21_Vol_1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Deimon High</a>, where everything is controlled by a single fearsome man, <s>Hiruma</s> Nixon!</b> School e</span>
  <span id="freeText17445407210812302128" style="display:none"><b>Welcome to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1087204.Ouran_High_School_Host_Club_Vol_01?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ouran High School</a>!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355408ra/9791557.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>A school for the children of the richest and most influential families in <s>Japan</s> America. One day, a poor <s>scholarship kid</s> contest winner will stumble across the <s>Host Club</s> Elect, a gang of gorgeous, influential and money-laden bastards, who then take her under their wing!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355408ra/9791558.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aft—what? *listens to earpiece* Oh, I'm sorry, I got it wrong. This isn't Ouran High School, it is, in fact, <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/832225.Eyeshield_21_Vol_1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deimon High</a>, where everything is controlled by a single fearsome man, <s>Hiruma</s> Nixon!</b> School equipment, people...anything you need, you just go right to him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355408ra/9791559.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I—what now? *listens to earpiece again* Sorry, folks, looks like there are some technical difficulties because I clearly heard Deimon High that time. Anyhow, turns out <b>this school is called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10626777-beelzebub-vol-01" rel="nofollow noopener">Ishiyama High</a>, commonly known as the school for delinquents because it's a super freaky place to study in! Near everyone there has a connection to the Underworld in some way and the best fighters run the school.</b> It's like a mafia Ouran High School.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, we can—oh for God's sake, what now? *rapid buzzing sounds from earpiece* Alright! Sorry <i>again</i>, people, it's actually <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/824763.Reborn_Vol_01?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Kokuyo Junior High</a>. <b>By some stroke of fate, a wimpy kid finds out he's next in line to be the boss of a very powerful mafia family.</b> He's soon forges connections with members of other mafia families and gets in fights with them too.<br><br><b>There's also a really scary guy who rules the school with an iron, um...<i>weapon</i>.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791561.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*static noise from earpiece* That's it, I give up! <i>You</i> talk to them.<br><br>Hey guys. Sorry about the confusion, though in my defense, this school sounds exactly like those so you can't really blame me for mixing them up. Anyways...<b>the school is actually named Eagle Elite university which basically takes all those above elements, that work great in the ridiculous, people-can-whip-mallets-from-panties fantastical setting of Japanese manga, and mashes them in a contemporary American university setting.</b> The result is a pile of uneatable goo. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355583ra/9791615.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, you may remember that I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/936569535" rel="nofollow noopener">praised Cracked</a> for doing the same thing, utilizing familiar concepts. However, Cracked is an urban fantasy/paranormal so it's entitled to a little reality-bending. Though you can bet that I'll call it out on its bullshit if it tries to pull the anime nosebleed or sweat gland gag on me.<br><br><b>Elite, on the other hand, is a contemporary novel,</b> meaning I expect a certain level of reality within. Although it doesn't contain ghosts or demons, <b>it failed to convince me that this is a college I could very well go to.</b><br><br>There's a gang of teenagers called the Elect and they're like the rulers of this majorly prestigious university. They control the elevators, the cafeteria, the gym...I bet they even control the rotation of the moon. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Don't even think about it, New Girl. You touch me, I tell the dean, who just so happens to be Phoenix's dad. We control the teachers because, guess what? My dad pays for everything."<br><br>"She won a silly contest. The same contest we put on every year so that the poor underprivileged people of the world are able to join the high society"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791563.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To be fair, I've never set foot in a American university so I'm not sure if that's how they really operate. Honestly doubt it, but let's not quibble. I do, however, study at the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Hong_Kong#Reputation_and_rankings" rel="nofollow noopener">arguably most prestigious university in Hong Kong</a> and I can tell you first-hand that we don't have anything like the Elect there. Everyone was all smiles on Orientation day, like in Monsters University.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791564.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, we do have a clique of kids from influential families and they have their own special dorm, but they don't throw their weight around. They just stick to themselves and throw wild parties. Or I assume.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Those problems aside, I wouldn't have enjoyed Elite anyway because <b>it read like the most cliche YA book in the world.</b> Or a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_" title="Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James" rel="nofollow noopener">Fifty Shades of Grey</a> rip-off. Same thing really.<br><br><b>Exhibit A: the gorgeous bad boy who treats the heroine horribly upon first meeting her, but ends up being the love interest.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"His face lit up with a smile, and honestly, it was like staring at an angel. Nixon was gorgeous. He was an ass, but gorgeous." <br><br>"He wore his perfection differently than most guys. The beauty of Nixon was in his imperfection. His crooked smile. The lip ring drew attention to his lips, making them look larger. And then his nose, it looked like it had been broken once, but it was in that tiny crook at the bridge that you saw something fierce in him. And his eyes. His ice blue eyes would warm within an instant when he was amused. His hair would fall across his brow giving him a rough yet vulnerable look."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Come on now. Can you look at that and tell me that doesn't look ripped straight out of a YA paranormal romance? <br><br>Nixon, the ravishing hero, is an asshole, end of story. <b>He humiliates the heroine, Trace, in public, sexually harasses her and commands her to eat and sit.</b> Hey there, Christian/Edward/Xavier! Long time no see!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/655358.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Like Katy Perry <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kTHNpusq654" rel="nofollow noopener">sings</a>, he's hot and he's cold! He's yes and he's no! Nixon shoves Trace up against an elevator wall when he feels like it and then leaves her hanging. He breaks up with her too cause it's <i>for her own good</i>. Hmm, where have I heard that before?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401355409i/9791566.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Exhibit B: the stupid heroine who falls for the jerk anyway.</b><br><br>I'll get this out of the way first—<b>Trace is an idiot. Not in an endearing way, but in a too-stupid-to-live way.</b> The Elite have been mean to her from day one and when one of them offers her a drink at a party, promising he didn't drug it, <b>she fucking drinks it.</b> Then she goes woozy and the guy carries her off as part of his grand scheme. I'm trying really hard not to victim-blame here, but Jesus-fucking-Christ, grow some brain cells! It's rule one of the Child Commandments: don't fucking take candy from strangers. <br><br>Also, rape culture:<br><br><b>RULE #8: Women should always accept and trust the kindness of strangers if they offer help. </b><br>That's for the above.<br><br>And this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I'd like to see someone mug me with him around."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>RULE #4: When in trouble, it is best to defer to the protection and judgment of men.</b><br>Other than Nixon, Chase, the friend-zoned guy (I'll get to him further along), protects Trace. Cause you know, us girls can't defend ourselves.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791567.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not going to go into the implications of rape culture here because this review would be a mile long if I did. Just keep those troubling signs in mind if you plan on reading Elite.<br><br>Right, back to our tstl heroine. <b>After all that verbal abuse, getting drugged and <i>egged</i>, she refuses to leave Eagle Elite.</b> I know she wants to make her Paw Paw proud or whatnot, but nothing is worth this. I'm sure her grandfather wouldn't want his beloved granddaughter to take this shit either. There's a big difference between bravery and plain old dumb. If you charge an armed army on your own with only a twig for protection, that's stupid, simple.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791568.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Trace is your typical YA blushing-bride heroine, flushing every other minute and becoming breathless.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Breathe. I just needed to breathe."<br><br>"A million different sensations ran through my body in that moment. It was nearly impossible to breathe."<br><br>"Was it possible for someone's head to heat up so much, it fell off their body?"<br><br>"Shivers ran up and down my arms at his absence.<br><br>Nixon released me and immediately, I felt so cold I shivered."</i>
</blockquote><br>Somebody get the girl a sweater before she catches pneumonia.<br><br>Trace acts like this before Nixon 'reforms'. The second he does, <b>she immediately falls into his arms, regardless of the shit he put her through before.</b><br><br>I actually like the bad-boy-with-a-heart-of-gold plotline. But if the guy treated the girl as horribly as he did Trace in the beginning, he has a lot of grovelling to do before I buy his transformation. And the girl needs to have some self-respect.<br><br>Since this book rips off so many mangas, I'm going to use to show you exactly how it should've went down. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5948514.Moe_Kare____Vol__01" title="Moe Kare!!, Vol. 01 by Go Ikeyamada" rel="nofollow noopener">Moe Kare!!, Vol. 01</a>, one of my favorite manga in the world, has a similar premise. It's about a girl, Hikaru, who's torn between two brothers. Extremely cheesy, I know, but that's not the point. One of the brothers, Arata, is very much like Nixon at the start. He's a womanizing bad boy and a complete jerk to Hikaru in the beginning. He steals her first kiss, sabotages Hikaru's relationship with the guy she likes, and insults her. Further in the story, he falls in love with her and wants her to be his girlfriend.<br><br>Unlike Trace, Hikaru doesn't fall into Arata's arms straight away. She distrusts him and with good reason, considering how mean he was to her in the past. Faced with this conundrum, Arata doesn't randomly shove Hikaru against an elevator wall and feel her up like Nixon. He takes action to redeem himself in Hikaru's eyes. He wakes up early to cook her meals, he comforts her when she cries, and even watches lame movies with her just cause she likes them. <b>It takes an entire month for Hikaru to reform her initial impression of Arata and become his girlfriend. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/675227.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>FYI, that's longer than Nixon and Trace have known each other.<br><br><b>That is what Nixon should have done and how Trace should have reacted. </b>Not go all weak-kneed like a newborn gazelle. Even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12578077.Obsidian__Lux___1_" title="Obsidian (Lux, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Obsidian</a> does a better job with the bad-boy-reformed trope than Elite does. <br><br><b>Trace is a Bella/Anastasia clone too.</b> Remember how Bella loves saying "Holy crow"? Well, looky here:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Holy superman."<br><br>"Holy crap." <br><br>"Holy hell." <br><br>"Holy football team."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Nice seeing you again, Bells. Now get out of my review space. <br><br><b>Exhibit C: Slut-shaming.</b><br><br>We've been seeing less and less of this in YA books lately, which is great. Yet the first NA book I pick up, I'm hit with this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Girls who looked more like my Barbie than a real person openly stared at me"<br><br>"If it was anything like the dress she was wearing now, then I was going to be put in prison for prostituting myself."<br><br>"Finally, she chose a purple dress with a plunging front and back. Only it was covered with some sheer material so technically it could not be defined as slutty. <br><br>I did say technically."<br><br>"She was ridiculously beautiful, making my mind immediately transport to every single book I'd read in the past year that warned me against girls who looked like her."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Tell me, Trace, what book did you read? Stereotypes 101? Just because someone's beautiful doesn't mean they like to get drunk and go bar-hopping.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398519690ra/9428555.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Exhibit D: a half-hearted love triangle for shits and giggles.</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I truly loved Nixon, but Chase...well, Chase had been my best friend for the past few weeks when Nixon was off fighting Phoenix and the evil of his family."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>It's your standard love triangle: a choice between the nice guy and dangerous dude. When <s>Edward</s> Nixon breaks Trace's heart, Chase is there to pick up the pieces. Same old, same old.<br><br>By the way, one of the awesome things about Moe Kare is that the girl goes with the friend-zoned guy in the end. The one who was there for her after the other shattered her heart. Team Arata, bitches.<br><br><b>Slightly irrelevant Exhibit E: Glamorizing of dangerous boys and dragging Taylor Swift into their shit.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Fine, it's just, Nixon reminds me of that Taylor Swift song, Trouble? You guys heard it?" I laughed as they all shook their heads. "Yeah, well, if I didn't know any better I'd think Nixon dated her, dumped her and she wrote a song about it."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>First, the song name is "I Knew You Were Trouble". Get your fucking facts straight. Second, <b>the song is a warning</b>. She's not telling you to date him. She's telling you run as far away from the guy as you can because you'll end up shamed and alone.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791569.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still don't believe me? In Taylor's album, the track before "I Knew You Were Trouble" is "Treacherous", a song about the attraction of dangerous love.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>CHORUS<br>This slope is treacherous<br>This path is reckless<br><b>This slope is treacherous<br>And I, I, I like it</b><br><br>Two headlights shine through the sleepless night<br>And I will get you, and get you alone<br>Your name has echoed through my mind<br>And I just think you should, think you should know<br><b>That nothing safe is worth the drive and I would<br>Follow you, follow you home...</b><br>I'll follow you, follow you home...</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Right after this ballad, we get the dubstep-ridden chords of "I Knew You Were Trouble" with Taylor singing:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I knew you were trouble when you walked in<br><b>So shame on me now</b><br>Flew me to places I'd never been<br>'Til you put me down, oh<br>I knew you were trouble when you walked in<br>So shame on me now<br>Flew me to places I'd never been<br><b>Now I'm lying on the cold hard ground</b><br>Oh, oh, trouble, trouble, trouble<br>Oh, oh, trouble, trouble, trouble</i>
</blockquote><br><br>A coincidence that the numbing consequences of bad decisions described by "I Knew You Were Trouble" comes right after the alluring seduction of risky love in "Treacherous"? I think not. Taylor put the two together for a reason. "I Knew You Were Trouble" is the aftermath of that kind of delusional love, and girls should GTFO before it screws them up. But Trace doesn't and gets her fucking HEA anyway. Way to educate the public.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401355409ra/9791570.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To conclude, a very disappointing introduction to the New Adult genre. If you know of any good ones, please rec them to me. This genre needs to be redeemed in my eyes.<br><br><i>ARC provided by Netgalley.</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17445407210812302128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2492178654" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16244808662765001792">This is my first Rachel Van Dyken read, and I know now that I need more of her in my life. For some reason, I thought Elite was some kind of military, political, or law enforcement type romance. I was very wrong lol, and I'm so glad! This was exactly what I needed last night when I picked it up. <br/><br/>Was it realistic? No...not at all. <br/><br/>Is the love triangle necessary? No.<br/><br/>Do I care? Nope! <br/><br/>I had so much fun reading it, and that's really all I wanted. It's super entertaining, well paced, and I enjoyed the</span>
  <span id="freeText16244808662765001792" style="display:none">This is my first Rachel Van Dyken read, and I know now that I need more of her in my life. For some reason, I thought Elite was some kind of military, political, or law enforcement type romance. I was very wrong lol, and I'm so glad! This was exactly what I needed last night when I picked it up. <br /><br />Was it realistic? No...not at all. <br /><br />Is the love triangle necessary? No.<br /><br />Do I care? Nope! <br /><br />I had so much fun reading it, and that's really all I wanted. It's super entertaining, well paced, and I enjoyed the writing style. I literally did not put it down until I finished. The only thing remotely negative I have to say is that I wish it had a little more steam, but overall, that's a tiny complaint. <br /><br />I winged this review, so I apologize if it's not the most cohesive or informative one you've ever read. I wanted to leave something though, because this book has mixed reviews amongst my goodreads friends. Hopefully, it will be helpful to someone in some way. <br /><br />Rachel Van Dyken definitely has my attention, and I can't wait to read more from her in the future. The Elite series just made it on my series to read in 2018 list. Elect here I come!</span>

<div id="review_590097770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590097770" />
    <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie"><img alt="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505392311p2/11641363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/590097770?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie " href="/user/show/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie">Christine Wallflower &amp; Dark Romance Junkie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=talk-dirty-to-me">talk-dirty-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=bloody-love-triangle">bloody-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=bossy-guys">bossy-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11641363-christine-wallflower-dark-romance-junkie?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590097770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7403487455293742689"><b>3 Elite Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406222720i/10521809.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Maybe the world isn't as shiny and fun as you once thought. People are mean. Humanity is a cruel joke, Trace. I'm just trying to prevent them from getting the last laugh."</i>
</b><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Let me explain</i>
</b><br/>____________________________________________<br/><br/>Every year Eagle Elite College, has a lottery. The winner gets an all expenses paid education at the college, this year the winner is, Trace Rooks. This is her opportunity to make her grandparents proud, b</span>
  <span id="freeText7403487455293742689" style="display:none"><b>3 Elite Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406222720i/10521809.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Maybe the world isn't as shiny and fun as you once thought. People are mean. Humanity is a cruel joke, Trace. I'm just trying to prevent them from getting the last laugh."</i>
</b><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>Let me explain</i>
</b><br>____________________________________________<br><br>Every year Eagle Elite College, has a lottery. The winner gets an all expenses paid education at the college, this year the winner is, Trace Rooks. This is her opportunity to make her grandparents proud, by going to Eagle Elite College she'll be set for life, she'll get the best job with the best salary. She's pretty excited until she gets to the school and is immediately knocked down a peg by a "group" called the Elite. They basically run the school, Nixon is the leader and what he says goes. If she doesn't conform, she suffers.<br><br>There are rules to follow:<br><b>1. Do not touch The Elect.<br>2. Do not look at The Elect.<br>3. Do not speak to The Elect.</b><br><br><i>*rolls eyes*</i><br>___________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>What did I think of this book?</i>
</b><br>___________________________________________<br><br>If you know me well, you'll know that I love outrageous plots with equally outrageous characters. Elite by Rachel Van Dyken only had one of these coveted points, I could have given this book five stars, I really would have. Why didn't I? Elite, had an unbelievable plot, that does not bother me. I found it all quite exciting. At first I wasn't really impressed with the characters, but hey I had time so I read on. And everything was going all hunky dory, until I realised it wasn't happening, I didn't like Trace or Nixon.<br><br>Nixon, was aloof and cold, and Trace... Trace was just dumb. There I said it, I'm fine and it's over. I can't begin to tell you at what point did Trace and Nixon decide they had feelings for each other. There was no build up, all of a sudden they were reciting sonnets (okay not sonnets) to each other and I was like WTF. Nixon's assholish behavior was far from cute and the fact that Trace never put up a fight was disappointing.<br><br>And then there was the Taylor Swift reference. The worst thing you could do in a book is mention an actual celebrity and then have said celebrity have a fictional relationship with a fictional character. I mean COME ON! Taylor Swift wrote Trouble because of Nixon. Look I no it's a book, but please go fly a flippin' kite!<br><br>I did like some parts of this book, I have this embarrassing thing I do. I love watching high school drama's with clicks and the awkward nerdy girl falling for the hot jock. So I was definitely entertained in the aspect although it wasn't exactly like that. Chase, is a side character that I loved, although I don't think he should be with Trace. I probably like him more than I do, Nixon.<br><br>This book lacked structure. Things just happened randomly and then they were over, and I was like HUH? I liked it when Nixon beat people up, I enjoyed it when they had to run from people shooting at them. I loved the excitement and supposed danger. I'm not sure why I'm giving this a three but I need to read the next book because I really need to know what happens next!<br><br><i>
  <b>I couldn't figure him out.<br>I don't think he even had himself figured out. <br>He was like a giant puzzle with broken and missing pieces.<br>And as much as I new I would regret it...I was on a hunt, for the missing and damaged ones. Every. Last. One.</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406222720i/10521810.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7403487455293742689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1928719225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1928719225" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392065462p2/18085807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1928719225?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18849991-elite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18085807-sabrina?shelf=college-new-adult-romance">college-new-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18085807-sabrina?shelf=mafia-crime-boss">mafia-crime-boss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1928719225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3458078816892398752"><b>Get it here:</b><br/><a href='https://amzn.to/3lGZ2YD' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon US</a> * <a href='https://amzn.to/3lC6TXg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon UK</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490419547ra/22311767.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I stupidly thought that this series was set in a High School, and that's why I always passed over it, but after hearing so many people praise it I just had to read it. And quickly realized that I was wrong and it's set in a very <u>elite</u> College, and that this was not a YA. <br/><br/>This book was honestly unlike any other that I've read, and I loved that it could give me something new to me and unique within the genre that I love. After reading as much as I do and f</span>
  <span id="freeText3458078816892398752" style="display:none"><b>Get it here:</b><br><a href="https://amzn.to/3lGZ2YD" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> * <a href="https://amzn.to/3lC6TXg" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a><br><br>3.5 Stars<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490419547ra/22311767.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I stupidly thought that this series was set in a High School, and that's why I always passed over it, but after hearing so many people praise it I just had to read it. And quickly realized that I was wrong and it's set in a very <u>elite</u> College, and that this was not a YA. <br><br>This book was honestly unlike any other that I've read, and I loved that it could give me something new to me and unique within the genre that I love. After reading as much as I do and for as long as I have, it's hard to find books that have a completely new plot that I've never heard of before. So if you're looking for something out-there and so crazy that you'll love it, <b>here it is!</b><br><br>The characters were interesting, a little annoying at times, but kept me captivated within their world. From the second I opened the book I had the need to know everything that was going on in this school and why Nixon acted the way he did. I really liked that I got so involved with the story and that it took over my life for my full day. <br><br>Overall, I'm seriously kicking myself for not reading reading this book sooner and I am not going to make the same mistake and wait too long to read the rest of the series. I did have a few issues with the heroine and I didn't like her that much, but it didn't make me hate the book. I would definitely recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3458078816892398752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_661945415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661945415" />
    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661945415?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781455554164" href="/book/show/18170509-elite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads?shelf=5-stars-favorites">5-stars-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661945415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2375432741115934622"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>OH.MY.GOD!!!!!! WHY DID IT TAKE ME SO LONG TO READ THIS?!!!!</b><br/><br/>I had no idea what Elite was about, I just knew it was a Dyken book and figured, light and fuffy? Well, it was so MUCH MORE!<br/><br/>It was adorable<br/><br/>It was intriguing<br/><br/>It was gripping<br/><br/>It was action pack<br/><br/>It was intense!<br/><br/><b>I LOVED IT!!!</b><br/><br/>Tracey got a scholarship into a very prestigious college. It’s not your typical college, they wear uniforms, there’s a class system with key cards and cliques. I actually just watched a Korean Drama that had a simila</span>
  <span id="freeText2375432741115934622" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>OH.MY.GOD!!!!!! WHY DID IT TAKE ME SO LONG TO READ THIS?!!!!</b><br /><br />I had no idea what Elite was about, I just knew it was a Dyken book and figured, light and fuffy? Well, it was so MUCH MORE!<br /><br />It was adorable<br /><br />It was intriguing<br /><br />It was gripping<br /><br />It was action pack<br /><br />It was intense!<br /><br /><b>I LOVED IT!!!</b><br /><br />Tracey got a scholarship into a very prestigious college. It’s not your typical college, they wear uniforms, there’s a class system with key cards and cliques. I actually just watched a Korean Drama that had a similar story line and I loved it, so Elite was a home-run for me too.<br /><br />Since Tracey is on scholarship, she’s kind of the odd duck out. Nixon is the head man on campus, everyone respects him and he kind of rules the school. For some reason, Nixon gives Tracy a hard time and she doesn’t know why.<br /><br />How adorable is the story line? Damsel in distress, Hero picking on the Heroine and Heroine just going through the emotions… yes please! I simply devour plots like these. The book was good from start to finish. The beginning was hilarious! Nixon did pretty mean things to Tracy and the things that were done to Tracy were just down right horrible, but in a funny good way. Who doesn’t want to read about a mob throwing eggs at the Heroine? <br /><br />Of course there’s a reason for everything and when you find out, the book only becomes more entertaining. Plot twist like these hold a place in my heart, I really do enjoy them. To me it’s like stepping into another world and I can just become a part of it. Let’s just say, Nixon is very mysterious and dangerous.<br /><br />I was never bored, I was never frustrated and I was entrained throughout. You want to know if there is a love triangle? Kind of… not really. There’s always the Hero’s best friend right? Chase is in the picture, but it’s really a small glimmer (something I can handle).<br /><br />Is there a cliffy? Not really, closed one. Will I go to book 2? HECK YEAH!<br /><br />I even love the cover, although it didn’t really tie in with the story, but the models were much better than the original. <br /><br />The down side of the book… realistic? No. Do I care? Hell no! Give me fantasy, thank you very much!<br /><br />It’s a great book and Dyken is amaze balls.<br /><br /><i>An ARC was provided in exchange for an honest review</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2375432741115934622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer593505940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9144132504379967875">OMG! This book was <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395714ra/762195.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I can't even begin to describe how much I loved it!<br/><br/>I saw this book a few weeks ago on Amazon and fell in love with the cover. Then I read the description. I was hooked. I was dying to read it. But…I couldn’t. I had a plan…a book plan. I had it planned out (through buddy reads) what I was going to read. So I put this off. But it wasn’t far from my mind. I thought about it daily. Then, I finished a book that was mentally exhausting. I could feel a book funk coming on. As I was f</span>
  <span id="freeText9144132504379967875" style="display:none">OMG! This book was <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395714ra/762195.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I can't even begin to describe how much I loved it!<br><br>I saw this book a few weeks ago on Amazon and fell in love with the cover. Then I read the description. I was hooked. I was dying to read it. But…I couldn’t. I had a plan…a book plan. I had it planned out (through buddy reads) what I was going to read. So I put this off. But it wasn’t far from my mind. I thought about it daily. Then, I finished a book that was mentally exhausting. I could feel a book funk coming on. As I was flipping through the pages of books on my kindle, I saw “Elite by Rachel Van Dyken” and decided to give it a try. From the first word, I was hooked. <br><br>Lol. I didn’t know whether I was supposed to love or hate Nixon and Chase when they were first introduced. I hated them for how they treated Trace but I was also intrigued. They made the book so much fun! (And it doesn’t hurt that they’re both hotties! ;) ) I honestly didn’t know who I liked more. And just when I thought I had it figured out, things would change on me. <br><br>I felt so bad for Trace. She was treated horribly by the other students at the school. I did like Monroe, she was a good friend. But part of me wishes we saw more of her. Poor Trace, she was completely in the dark. Everyone was keeping secrets from her. But I enjoyed her as a heroine. <br><br>This book had me laughing, had my heart racing and even breaking with the events that occurred. I couldn’t think of a better book to read. This was perfect. I have to say, the author did an amazing job. I can’t wait for more books from this series and I’ll be buying up all her existing books as soon as this review is posted. She has a new fan and she is a new auto-buy author for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/533204.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I could, I would give this book more than 5 stars. One last thought: If you haven’t read this yet, go read it. It’s a great book that will keep you hooked. <br><br>My Nixon: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418088i/827569.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My Chase: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380418088i/827570.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>My reviews can also be found on <a href="http://confessionsof2booklovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Confessions of 2 Book Lovers.</a></span>

<div id="review_606970082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/606970082" />
    <a title="Ivie dan Glokta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta"><img alt="Ivie dan Glokta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441134469p2/9838687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/606970082?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivie dan Glokta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivie dan Glokta" href="/user/show/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta">Ivie dan Glokta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta?shelf=absoute-shaite">absoute-shaite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta?shelf=bullsh-t">bullsh-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9838687-ivie-dan-glokta?shelf=insulted-intelligence">insulted-intelligence</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer606970082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15570616105742189854">By chapter two i knew i would hate this book, by chapter five i wanted to throw my reader against the wall.<br/><br/>This story was so over the top it might as well been pulled out the authors ass then written.<br/><br/>This is a revised version of my original review. I just had to come back to it, it was bugging me THAT MUCH.<br/><br/>My original review was a rant of just a few key points of the novel that I had issues with. But now a few days and conversations later I am ready to properly explain why I hated this book so m</span>
  <span id="freeText15570616105742189854" style="display:none">By chapter two i knew i would hate this book, by chapter five i wanted to throw my reader against the wall.<br /><br />This story was so over the top it might as well been pulled out the authors ass then written.<br /><br />This is a revised version of my original review. I just had to come back to it, it was bugging me THAT MUCH.<br /><br />My original review was a rant of just a few key points of the novel that I had issues with. But now a few days and conversations later I am ready to properly explain why I hated this book so much.<br /><br />I would usually start at the beginning and work my way on but there is one paragraph that I would like to quote.<br /><br /><i>“Chase shrugged. “He’s not just in charge of the key cards, he’s student body president. He makes sure that access is limited for each student. Take for example, a kid from North Korea going to school here. You think they’re going to get along with a South Korean? Or better yet, some ritzy American kid?”<br />“Um… no?”<br />Everyone laughed.<br />Phoenix shook his head. “That’s a hell no, New Girl.”</i><br /><br />Well done van Dyken... <br />Now for those of you that haven't yet read this book this paragraph refers to Nixon, our leading man in the novel. He is a student that is student body president and somehow manages to teach a class as well. That is nothing to get worked up about, but however the fact that he is in charge of all of the administration, gets to decide who lives where, who eats when and how much is. Another example : <i>“He reached into his pocket and pulled out a blue key card and dangled it in front of me. “Say thank you.”<br />“For what?” I would not cry. I would not cry!<br />“Allowing you to eat, of course.”<br />“What?”<br />“I’m not finished talking,” he said smoothly. “This key card gains you access into the elevator only once a week. It also gains you access into the cafeteria, twice a day. Not three times. We don’t want you gaining weight. Use it wisely and if you impress me with your ability to follow directions. I may just up your freedom. Until then…” He shrugged and cleared his throat. “Move aside.”</i><br /><br />I shall return to Nixon shortly right after the Korea disaster. Now this is a school right? And in this school you might find children that are the sons and daughters of diplomats and politicians but that is just it. They are, and to quote van Dyken herself -<b>KIDS!!!!</b> Van Dyken angled to prove just how exclusive this place is by adding bits of real life to it, with absolutely no research what so ever. But just in case I wasn't overreacting because of fictional characters I decided to ask for the opinion of my very real, very South Korean colleague. After the initial <u>'the b*tch said what?'</u> look, she greeted that particular nugget with two middle fingers raised and a bunch of profanities I chose not to repeat. Long story short, that paragraph made as much sense as saying you can't have a Catholic in the same room as a Muslim. I bet she got the idea watching the evening news one night when North Korea was mentioned. The author wanted to imprint the exclusivity and the importance of her characters but had not thought of how to achieve it that she shot off the first thing that came to mind, and not even bothering to think on how little sense it all made. If she did, she would realise just how unbelievable ranting about some random kid making school cafeteria seating schedule for the benefit of all mankind and world peace really is, or how offensive it would be to label people based on their nationalities alone. That last one by the way......is a big NO-NO.<br /><br />Now the rest of it...Jesus, where even to begin?<br /><br />Lets just stick to Trace and Nixon. <br /><br />Trace, as the author wants us to believe is an innocent as flowers little farm girl. So innocent that she refers to hair curlers as <i>“weird rod thingy”</i>. I would even believe it if she wouldn't refer to the guys in the next chapter as GQ models or <i>“having nothing on Tommy Hilfiger”</i>. So she knows about models and fashion, but has never heard of hair curlers? Right, another believable and thought- trough moment there. Secondly she gets nothing but abuse but she never has any real emotions involved. Her emotional response is about a sentence long. She gets drugged with a date rape drug and dumped in some random guys bed and she just gets up and gets on with her day? Huh? <br /><br />That is not cool. That is not how any woman on this planet would feel and most certainly that is NOT OK! She is not a naïve little farm girl-she is a moron.<br /><br />Nixon is the biggest fail in this book. With him the author went for all or nothing and would up with a smelly carcass achieved by an overkill of her vivid imagination. He looks and acts like a GOD, he speaks ten languages, he is single-handedly responsible for the peace between the kids in school therefore in the world by his very politically correct lunch seating arranging skills. He is student body president and a teacher. I mean Superman move the phuck over, we got Nixon in the house.His real traits however are as sad as can be. He is self obsessed and an abusive asshole. <br /><br />This book is a disaster. The author gave it an honest try but failed in every aspect that counts. She did no research whatsoever and it shows. If it's not a cliché upon a cliché then its absolute and utter nonsense. The conversation between the characters was so immature, the alleged humor was so childish and forced it was like reading a kid's first attempt at writing an essay. Why did i still go trough it? Let's just say that this particular novel was like a bizarre accident, you know what your eyes are seeing is horrific but you just cannot seem to be able to look away.<br /><br />There are more things about this book that just don't add up but it's just not worth the mentioning. Suffice to say that the sheer amount of idiocies in these pages are enough to make the experience of reading them painful. They flow trough your mind like salted sandpaper on a burn.<br /><br />Congrats van Dyken, you just made to the top of my I won't read that sh*t list.<br /><br /> What a waste of money this was. I could have had my fave coffee at Starbucks instead.... damn</span>
  <a data-text-id="15570616105742189854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1077069086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077069086" />
    <a title="☆ Sammy ☆彡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14144676-sammy"><img alt="☆ Sammy ☆彡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462053159p2/14144676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1077069086?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆ Sammy ☆彡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆ Sammy ☆彡" href="/user/show/14144676-sammy">☆ Sammy ☆彡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18849991-elite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14144676-sammy?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14144676-sammy?shelf=mafia">mafia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1077069086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2981902499546673071">Elite was my first novel by Rachel Van Dyken. Having heard so many wonderful things about her Ruin series and being intrigued by the blurb, I decided to jump into this book relatively blind. As a whole, I really enjoyed the story but unfortunately there were aspects of this book that left me with mixed feelings. <br/><br/><b>What I Liked:</b><br/><br/>I had a hard time putting this book down =) The plot kept me engaged and I was really intrigued by all the mystery surrounding the university and its students. I wanted to k</span>
  <span id="freeText2981902499546673071" style="display:none">Elite was my first novel by Rachel Van Dyken. Having heard so many wonderful things about her Ruin series and being intrigued by the blurb, I decided to jump into this book relatively blind. As a whole, I really enjoyed the story but unfortunately there were aspects of this book that left me with mixed feelings. <br><br><b>What I Liked:</b><br><br>I had a hard time putting this book down =) The plot kept me engaged and I was really intrigued by all the mystery surrounding the university and its students. I wanted to know what was really going on with the school and why the students, especially Nixon, were so secretive and acted so horribly to Trace.<br><br>Trace is a character that I had an easy time relating too. Like her, I would have been intimidated moving from a small farm in Wyoming and starting college at an elite, ivy league school like Eagle Elite University. I really respected Tracey's strength of character. I mean, the snobs at the university treated her like garbage and did everything in their power to make Trace believe that she didn't belong but she wouldn't let them break her. She stayed focused on school, refused to be pushed around, and even responded to everyone's hostility with witty comebacks and sarcasm.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413813993i/11566304._SY540_.jpg" height="350" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What I Struggled With:</b><br><br>When all the answers to my questions were finally revealed, I was little disappointed. Nixon's reasoning never justified his behavior and I still don't completely understand why he had to be such an asshole to Trace. <br><br>This brings me to the next aspect of the story that I struggled with: Nixon's character. Don't get me wrong, I love my fair share of literary bad boys but I almost found Nixon's behavior non-redeemable. My feelings for him might have been different had his justification made more sense to me. <br><br>The last thing that I had an issue with involved the story's structure. The way everything was revealed in the end, combined with all of the action, I felt like the ending was a bit rushed. If all the secrets had came out a little earlier in the story, it would have given me more time to digest the information and would have decreased the level of frustration I felt throughout most of the book.<br><br><b>Final Thoughts:</b><br><br>Elite by Rachel Van Dyken was definitely a page turner for me. I was hooked by the intrigue, the secrets, a strong heroine, and forbidden romance between Trace and Nixon. I will be continuing the series because, even though I had some mixed feelings, I was still thinking about this book and these characters days after I finished reading and I really want to see how everything works out in the end. <br><br><i>ARC courtesy of the publisher, Forever (Grand Central Publishing), via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2981902499546673071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
