<div id="review_597481262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597481262" />
    <a title="Rooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18553-rooks"><img alt="Rooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379140016p2/18553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/597481262?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rooks" href="/user/show/18553-rooks">Rooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer597481262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9172452598661109853">Ok, here's the thing - this book was candy. Moderately tasty candy, more than a little improbable candy, but you know, sometimes you just want candy. I feel like it's more of a 2.5 - while the plotting pushes me towards a 2, the fact that I read it in one sitting pushes me towards a 3. After typing everything out, I'm giving it the 2, mostly because if someone walked up to me and asked me what I thought of this book, I would say, "It was ok." Those are the exact words that would leave my lips. I</span>
  <span id="freeText9172452598661109853" style="display:none">Ok, here's the thing - this book was candy. Moderately tasty candy, more than a little improbable candy, but you know, sometimes you just want candy. I feel like it's more of a 2.5 - while the plotting pushes me towards a 2, the fact that I read it in one sitting pushes me towards a 3. After typing everything out, I'm giving it the 2, mostly because if someone walked up to me and asked me what I thought of this book, I would say, "It was ok." Those are the exact words that would leave my lips. It was rather readable, but many caveats, etc.<br><br>Like what, you ask? OK!<br><br>The initial premise of Elite is basically a wholesale ripoff of Boys Over Flowers (a manga/tv show from Japan/South Korea). It doesn't <i>stay</i> straight unoriginal, BUT STILL.* <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406563ra/793375.gif" width="300" height="164" alt="nerd rage" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>It just bothers me, ok?</i><br><br>Right, so like I was saying, Elite begins as a BoF knockoff, but instead of an elite (heh) high school cum college, it's just a college. (An American college where they make you wear uniforms to class? Okaaaaaaaay.) Many of the initial plot points are near carbon copies - the main heroine winning the proverbial (or in this case, literal) lottery and becoming the token outsider kid in a world of richy-rich douchebaggery all for the sake of the untold opportunity said college provides, her getting hazed via egging and thereby having her one super-fancy uniform ruined, the initial acrimonious run-ins with a clique of four super hot dudes born to immense privilege wherein the hottest one is both the leader and the biggest asshole of them all (at first), the bonding with the super-nice model (or hot enough to be a model) lady affiliated with that clique, blahblahblah. It's westernized and eventually mobbed up, but yeah, it's the same.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829272.gif" width="300" height="225" alt="BoF" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>This, but with Sicilian-Americans.</i><br><br>That mobbed up bit is where it gets interesting, and also problematic. I'm honestly not sure why it took Trace so long to figure out the mob thing. Seriously. Despite the fact that she seems reasonably intelligent, I wanted to buy this girl a clue on more than one occasion. (Since this book is actually on a goodreads list for mob stories, I don't consider this a spoiler.) Also, when prompted, Trace can find her spine, but (full disclosure) I tend to prefer protagonists who can be even modestly badass without being pushed to it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829273.gif" width="300" height="167" alt="milquetoast" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I really don't believe you, like at all.</i><br><br>Also, there are things that sort of don't make sense, like who is pissed at who is sort of evident, but the rationale behind the obvious why is a bit of a headscratcher, which is a problem because all of this Cosa Nostra drama is informing the actions of the characters in ways that also sometimes don't make sense. Taking this a step further, in the context of the main character being a bit milquetoasty, then, the end makes sense. Sort of. In the context of this being a mob book, the end REALLY DOES NOT MAKE SENSE. NOT EVEN A LITTLE BIT. The cliffhanger ending has an <i>incredibly simple solution</i>, but in order for it to actually be a cliffhanger, it looks like no one's gonna go ahead and handle their business accordingly. (Sorry to be all oblique, but I'm trying to keep it entirely spoiler free.) As I was reading this book, I couldn't help but think, "Umm, Michael Corleone would SCHOOL THESE BITCHES." Because he would. He really, really would. For realsies.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829274.gif" width="300" height="169" alt="godfather" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I'm sorry, what was I saying?</i><br><br>And yes, of course I was more than a little annoyed by the whole "girls need rescuing" thing at the end. (Actual Quote: "Stupid girls. We always need rescuing.") I think it was supposed to be cute or something, but c'mon now. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829275.gif" width="300" height="155" alt="killself" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Props for being explicit with it, I guess?</i><br><br>What else is there to say?** Shit is bothersome. Finis.<br><br>But no, not finis, because I can't finish talking about this - and this is a way longer review than I intended - without discussion of the love "triangle". SIGH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829276.gif" width="300" height="173" alt="awhellnaw" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Upon discovering most love triangles.</i><br><br>Why the scare quotes? Because it is SO. DAMN. FORCED. I know love triangles are the thing to do, or whatever, but I feel like Trace and Nixon have enough interesting potential problems (like the fact that dude's name is Nixon - can you imagine yelling that out in bed?) with their relationship and with the world at large to not need a monkey wrench that even the author describes as a poor man's version of the male Lurv Interest. We all already know who The One is, so let's not kid ourselves. If I never read another love triangle simply for the sake of having a love triangle, it will be too soon.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380418681ra/829277.gif" width="300" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>After reading most love triangles.</i><br><br>But yeah, other than all of that, candy-ish? I guess? I'll probably read the next one if I stumble across it, and it was interesting enough for me to check out some of this author's other work - she writes a good make out scene - but not enough to make my autoyes list by any means.<br><br>---<br>*<i>At this juncture, you may be asking yourself, what the hell kind of random, grown-up USAmerican would randomly know enough about a teenage Korean TV show that aired for three months four years ago to know that this book is copying off of that show's test page? And so I answer, someone who watches A LOT of Netflix and then follows her late night viewing down the rabbit hole of the Internet via the gateway drug that is Wikipedia. Seriously, go watch the first episode on Netflix - never fear, it's subtitled - and tell me the premise is not the same; this review will be here when you get back.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/607158.gif" width="300" height="169" alt="sherlock research" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>There's always time for research!</i><br><br>**Patriarchy, etc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9172452598661109853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/665990338" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8278010-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352109855p2/8278010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/665990338?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/8278010-jo">Jo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer665990338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9519018478188069631"><br/>Ok, where do I start?<br/>This book turned out not I was expecting at all and not in a good way!<br/>I do love when an author tries to think outside the box and gives us a fresh take in what could have been the same old formula.<br/><br/>So Trace won a scholarship for the most exclusive college in the world, the college where the kids from the most influential and powerful people in the world go to aka Eagle Elite College.<br/>So to Trace, a farm girl, to win the scholarship, it was like to win the lottery...<br/><br/>Only to dis</span>
  <span id="freeText9519018478188069631" style="display:none"><br>Ok, where do I start?<br>This book turned out not I was expecting at all and not in a good way!<br>I do love when an author tries to think outside the box and gives us a fresh take in what could have been the same old formula.<br><br>So Trace won a scholarship for the most exclusive college in the world, the college where the kids from the most influential and powerful people in the world go to aka Eagle Elite College.<br>So to Trace, a farm girl, to win the scholarship, it was like to win the lottery...<br><br>Only to discovered a new world, where the Elects rule the all school and you must follow their biding or suffer the consequences...<br><br>Now what did bother me in this story?<br>Many things actually!<br><br>First one, almost half all the book I had this deja vu feeling...there were LOADS of similarities between this story and Korean drama I watches years ago, <b> Boys Before Flowers</b>, that was based on the japanese manga Hana Yori Dango. <br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/585/tumblrmfrm1osrg81rjpxgs.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428946ra/858841.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I felt that Elite was like an american version of it, the 4 gorgeous and handsome Elect that rule the college, rang a bell form my old friends F4. <br>The wining a scholarship, the bullying, to the leader falling in love with the poor girl...and of course rescuing her from all the other students trowing her eggs and so on.<br><br>Then why, if i did enjoyed the drama I didn't liked it in this story? <br>Well, basically because regarding a drama (especially one based in a manga) we have to expect some over the top scenes or story lines or even ridiculous ones. To read it in a new adult story, not so much!<br><br>***spoilers***<br><br>What did bother me, was that this was a college setting, ages 18 to over...and it appeared like some High School for me. And still wearing uniforms, really?<br><br>Now, he are introduce to a whole Mafia story line. <br>Nixon is the ultimate Boss and also the leader of the Elect. So basically he runs the school...Am I to believe that someone that have to run all the business in the familia is wasting time at college to rule the school? I do get it was in his plan to undercover some truths but still...<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/20/v5o.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380428946ra/858842.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I didn't connected with the characters and I didn't felt most of the romance. Plus the whole revelation I loved you since I was 9 years old, not realistic :( Close friends or someone you would always trust? Sure! But the love of your life,hmmmmm....<br>The more I think about this story, the more frustrated I get...There were some scenes that I enjoyed but when I expected to get better it didn't.<br>To sum it up, in my opinion, this story was just all over the place...and it was just infuriating that nearly by the end of the story, trowing a love triangle like that, REALLY? REALLY?<br><br><br>Anyway, this was just not the book for me :(<br><br><br>***egalley kindly provided via Netgalley in exchange of an honest review ***<br></span>

    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32445724-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551516258p2/32445724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2806915823?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/32445724-wendy">Wendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32445724-wendy?shelf=college">college</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32445724-wendy?shelf=mafia">mafia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32445724-wendy?shelf=mild-steam">mild-steam</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32445724-wendy?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2806915823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1882317785303934561">I had read some books in this series already, but for some reason, I skipped the first books. I am known to read the books in series assbackwards, so I am not surprised. I figured it was time to fix it though...especially since I have started the new spin-0ff. <br/><br/>I didn't enjoy it as much as the later books in the series I have to say. I think the biggest reason for this is the fact that I really did not like Trace... sorry not sorry. <br/><br/>She was not my type of heroine. The constant crying and the igno</span>
  <span id="freeText1882317785303934561" style="display:none">I had read some books in this series already, but for some reason, I skipped the first books. I am known to read the books in series assbackwards, so I am not surprised. I figured it was time to fix it though...especially since I have started the new spin-0ff. <br /><br />I didn't enjoy it as much as the later books in the series I have to say. I think the biggest reason for this is the fact that I really did not like Trace... sorry not sorry. <br /><br />She was not my type of heroine. The constant crying and the ignorance. I also don't like it when a woman is reduced to nothing but a body. Like they can't think straight anymore because their bodies are so drawn to the anti hero. They keep going on and on about how their bodies are betraying them.... really starting to annoy me. <br /><br />Thankfully I did like all the other characters in this book, especially Chance, but I have already read his story (which I loved btw). <br /><br />Now I want to read about Phoenix, he was quite the villain in this one and I want to see if he can redeem himself in my eyes. Since I am not a big Trace fan, I think this shouldn't be hard...also I love me a cruel asshole :P <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1882317785303934561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_661973015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/661973015" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/661973015?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781455554164" href="/book/show/18170509-elite">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer661973015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18068906365811071682">How do I write a reaction to Rachel Van Dyken's "Elite"? I guess on one hand, you could say this was trying to be a humorous, thrilling romantic read in the scheme of New Adult, but it rubbed me the wrong way for the utter implausibilities in the storyline. I had a hard time getting through much of it because it seemed like a poorly written version of the YA series "Private" by Kate Brian, or even a poorer version of the anime/manga series Hana Yori Dango (Boys Over Flowers). And then it transit</span>
  <span id="freeText18068906365811071682" style="display:none">How do I write a reaction to Rachel Van Dyken's "Elite"? I guess on one hand, you could say this was trying to be a humorous, thrilling romantic read in the scheme of New Adult, but it rubbed me the wrong way for the utter implausibilities in the storyline. I had a hard time getting through much of it because it seemed like a poorly written version of the YA series "Private" by Kate Brian, or even a poorer version of the anime/manga series Hana Yori Dango (Boys Over Flowers). And then it transitioned to something more that I couldn't follow for the utter over the top drama it held.<br /><br />The story revolves around Trace, a young woman who moved from Wyoming to attend an elite college after winning some kind of draw/contest (don't ask me - it was in the book, it was a weird place to start from). As the new girl (or "Farm Girl" as she's called), she's subjected to so many hazing rituals on the part of the Elite, who pretty much rule every aspect of the school including holding key cards which control how much the heroine has to eat and live off of in the facilities of the school. She gets drawn between the affections of the guys who are supposedly the "king bees" of this institution and are among the privileged few. I had a really hard time believing these students had so much control over the teachers and access to things around this institution. It drove me a little stir crazy as I read through it because I couldn't suspend disbelief at the establishment being what it was.<br /><br />The heroine gets subjected to not only being drugged and made to think she slept with one of the Elect (and gets called names and petty labels for the insinuation), but also becomes the butt of several sexually harassing gestures and creepy come-ons that made me cringe as I read through the work. And the heroine has some kind of weird association with cows that was repeated over and over in a way that wasn't endearing at all.<br /><br />And the larger conflict? I had to shake my head at the convoluted associations it made with mob mentalities and murder and just...I couldn't. I just couldn't.<br /><br />But apart from that, this is pretty much your typical New Adult novel for cliches - uber jerk love interest, heroine who pines for hero despite him being a jerk, female-female hating, slut-shaming, bitch-slamming...wash, rinse, repeat. Argh. And this was one of those books I really hoped would be different.<br /><br />I can't say I have a handle on Rachel Van Dyken's style of writing yet (Her prose in itself is compulsively readable - I finished this fairly quickly for time, but it contained a lot of grammatical errors for tenses, comma use, among other measures - more than it should've had even for a galley), but it's probably better I stop with this respective series because I had too many issues with it. It was not fun in the least.<br /><br />Overall score: 0.5/5 stars<br /><br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher Forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18068906365811071682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_592068235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592068235" />
    <a title="Belle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9419782-belle"><img alt="Belle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592068235?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belle" href="/user/show/9419782-belle">Belle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=truly-madly-deeply-in-love">truly-madly-deeply-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=dealing-with-issues">dealing-with-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=cool-kids-on-the-block">cool-kids-on-the-block</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=hot-leading-men">hot-leading-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=hero-saves-the-day">hero-saves-the-day</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592068235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3058018484556910402"><i>
  <b>“—Nope. You’ve already broken a rule. I’m speaking, New Girl.” Chase smirked. “Geez, Nixon, this one’s going to be hard to break in.”<br/>“They always are,” Nixon replied, lifting my chin with his hand. “But I think I’ll enjoy this one.”</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>Wow.<br/><br/>What did I just read.<br/><br/>That book was not what I expected at all.</b><br/><br/>This book was engaging, terrifying, suspenseful, romantic, utterly depressing and heart-wrenching all at the same time. It feels like my heart got handed to me on a platter… I need the next book NOW</span>
  <span id="freeText3058018484556910402" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“—Nope. You’ve already broken a rule. I’m speaking, New Girl.” Chase smirked. “Geez, Nixon, this one’s going to be hard to break in.”<br />“They always are,” Nixon replied, lifting my chin with his hand. “But I think I’ll enjoy this one.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>Wow.<br /><br />What did I just read.<br /><br />That book was not what I expected at all.</b><br /><br />This book was engaging, terrifying, suspenseful, romantic, utterly depressing and heart-wrenching all at the same time. It feels like my heart got handed to me on a platter… I need the next book NOW. Hopefully "cross fingers" it comes out soon.<br /><br />This book follows the story of a girl who wins a competition and gains acceptance in one of the country's most prestigious schools… this sounds familiar to all you YA followers right ? Think this book will be like Gossip Girl ? Hell no. In this book it is not the girls who rule the school, but the boys, and let me tell you the boys can be just as vicious and cruel as the girls. Here the school is led by a group called the "Elect", and the one who rules them all is a dark haired, tall, utterly gorgeous, wonderful and cruel male specimen called Nixon. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Here the rules are clear: <br /><br />1. Do not touch The Elect.<br /><br />2. Do not look at The Elect.<br /><br />3. Do not speak to The Elect.</i>
</b><br /><br />But of course, what good story would this be if the girl followed all these rules and became a nobody. No of course Trace rebelled against the rules and got everyone, including Nixon, to notice her… popularity is not always a good thing. Nixon rules the school, yet Trace can not seem to figure out why. But somethings are best kept secret and in amidst a coming of age story, something dangerous is lurking in the shadows, in this case the dark secret Nixon is holding may be the key in unravelling it all.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Nixon smelled like hot guy. Seriously, they should bottle him up and put him in stores. He’d make millions, not that he needed it.</i>
</b><br /><br />Now I will tell you right now, this book really did truly surprise me. In a good way. I was expecting a typical new adult drama, but was given something entirely different and shockingly quite sinister. The secret he holds should have been expected and it made sense with a lot of the signs pointing to it, but even when it was revealed I still had my "Oh no he didn't just say that" face on. I mean let me say Dyken is very clever in the whole "you think you know what the secret is, but you really don't" game. <br /><br />The were my initial thoughts:<br /><i> "What the." <br />"No Way"<br />"But he… But that"<br />"HOW?"<br />"Ohhhh.."<br />Ohhhhhhhhhh"<br />Okay"<br />"Oh yeah, that makes sense."<br />"Knew it."<br />"Saw that coming a mile away. " :) </i><br /><br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Mafia boss. Sicilian… you know the typical hidden dark secret in a new adult story.. NAHTTTT!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Nixon’s smile was sad. “I love you, Trace. I always have. Just remember that, okay? Hold on to it. No matter what I say or what I do… and trust me, I’ll do some terrible things. Just know. I love you. With every fiber of my being.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I won't lie the secret made me even more excited to read the book. What can I say I love dangerous, possessive, crazy lead males.<br />Her naivety at points made me want to scream at her I won't lie, but I loved Trace's guts. And did I mention Chase another seriously attractive, funny lead male… wish my uni was crowded with boys as hot as these. (maybe not characteristically, but in looks only) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ LOVE TRIANGLE ANYONE? totally saw that coming  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Skittles?” I repeated.<br />“He wants you to taste the rainbow.” Nixon groaned. “It's one of his lines, and then he puts the skittles in his mouth and kisses you. It’s a very tired line that he can’t seem to let go of, huh, Chase?”<br />“Bastard,” Chase joked and went about putting our snacks together.</i>
</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ AND WHAT WAS WITH THE PROLOGUE SNEAK PEEK FOR THE NEXT BOOK… TRACE WHAT ARE YOU DOING. CHASE OR NIXON?!! IM CONFUSSEEEDD! We literally just ended the first book with a happy nixon and trace love-y dove-y moment, and now we are wrapped up in another man's arms? Now I just have to see how this pans out..  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Nixon didn’t kiss as if it was something to pass the time. He kissed as if there was nothing in the world he’d rather be doing. He kissed like I was his oxygen, and I knew in that moment there was no way I was ever letting him go for the second time.</i>
</b><br /><br />DEFINITE RECOMMEND to those who love dangerous, action, thriller, suspenseful, romantic type novels. Not for those who want "realistic" type drama. But who really wants that kind of drama half the time anyway. (Word.) 4.5/5!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3058018484556910402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>**ARC courtesy of Forever (Grand Central Publishing) via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review**</i>

  <span id="freeText2366747771736644992" style="display:none"><br><br><br><b>
  <i>**ARC courtesy of Forever (Grand Central Publishing) via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review**</i>
</b><br><br><b>3,5 find-out-who-you-really-are STARS!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428822i/858345.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you have read the synopsis of this book you already know how cryptic this story is... and well, you won't really find out what's really going on completely until almost the end of the book. <br><br>Why?<br><br>Because this is only <b>the first book of the series Eagle Elite and it's all about solving the mystery</b> while you read :) <br><br>So I'm not gonna go into too much detail and describe the plot, just introduce the story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428822i/858346.jpg" width="400" height="460" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Those are the <b>rules Trace needs to follow if she wants to survive and graduate in one of the most elitist schools in Chicago</b>. She was raised in a farm and thanks to a lottery she has a opportunity to change her future. But who is the Elect? <br><br><b>Nixon, a handsome mysterious boy, threatens to make Trace's life hell if she doesn't follow those rules</b> and treats him like the "king" the rest of the students consider him. But he claims that what he actually means is to protect her...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428822i/858347.jpg" width="400" height="266" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Trace has to suffer really horrible things while she tries to adapt... but what neither she or Nixon expect is what fate has in store for them. <br><b>Unexpected secrets will be revealed and romance will be present.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428822i/858348.jpg" width="400" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380428822i/858349.jpg" width="400" height="282" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I really enjoyed reading this book</b>, it was an easy read and it kept me hooked at all times. <b>Characters were good</b> and though both those and the story were a total mystery, I really liked how little by little I got to discover what was going on. I also like the fact that this is a series and <b>many questions are still to be answered in the next books.</b><br>The "secret" was a surprise, I didn't really expect anything like that when I started reading the book, but everything was pretty well linked. Still, I found some of the happenings a little bit surreal... probably because I'm not used to reading books with that topic <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[mafia <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and don't enjoy them as much as a regular YA. <br><br>Anyways, I'm sure the story will get a lot better in the next book, I expect a lot more romance, angst and steamy moments ;) especially now that I think <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a love triangle is happening <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> :P</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16384880111109810940">Arc provided by Netgalley<br/><br/><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>DNF at 5%<br/><br/>Yes, 5%..because with only five percent read, there was:<br/>_Clumsy narration, if Trace is such a genius i was expecting something more fluent than this:<br/><br/><i>The buildings were huge. Everything was built in old stone and brick. I mean, I’d seen pictures, but they did not even come close to reality. The dorms looked like ritzy hotels.</i><br/><br/>_Overabuse of cheesiness....<br/><br/><i>I gave grandpa a watery smile as he reached across the console and grasped my hand within his large worn one</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16384880111109810940" style="display:none">Arc provided by Netgalley<br><br><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>DNF at 5%<br><br>Yes, 5%..because with only five percent read, there was:<br>_Clumsy narration, if Trace is such a genius i was expecting something more fluent than this:<br><br><i>The buildings were huge. Everything was built in old stone and brick. I mean, I’d seen pictures, but they did not even come close to reality. The dorms looked like ritzy hotels.</i><br><br>_Overabuse of cheesiness....<br><br><i>I gave grandpa a watery smile as he reached across the console and grasped my hand within his large worn one. He’d sacrificed everything for me, so I was going to do this for him, for grandma. It may sound silly but being an only child I felt this immense need to take care of him now that grandma was gone, and the only way I could see myself doing that was getting a good job and making him proud. I wasn’t sure about his retirement, or about anything, and I wanted to be. I wanted to take care of him, like he took care of me.<br>He was my rock, and now it was my turn to be his.<br>Grandpa winked and squeezed my hand again. He was always so perceptive. I could tell he knew I was thinking about grandma</i><br><br>Also, the same old patterns when new girl(or boy) enters a college have become tiresome:<br>Disdain thrown in by the girls..<br>Provocation done by the boys...<br><br>BUT....what i can't force myself to read is <b>sexual harassment situations</b>.<br><br>It is said that Trace was home schooled...therefore she is seen as this innocent, poor little girl who can't defend herself against this f****k!<br><br>They only met, and he's doing and saying this??<br><br><i>“No,” Nixon answered for Chase. This time his touch was smooth as he caressed my arm. I tried to jerk away. His face lit up with a smile, and honestly, it was like staring at a fallen angel. Nixon was gorgeous. He was an ass, but he was a gorgeous ass. “You feel this?”<br>His hand continued moving up my arm until he reached my shoulder, and then his hand moved to my neck and his thumb grazed my trembling lips. “Memorize it now, because as of this moment, you<br>can’t touch us. We are untouchable. If you as much as sneeze in our direction, if you as much breathe the same air in my atmosphere, I will make your life hell. This touch, what you feel against your skin, will be the only time you feel another human being as powerful as me near you. So like I said, feel it, remember it, and maybe one day, your brain will do you the supreme favor of forgetting what it felt like to have someone like me touching you. Then, and only then, will<br>you be able to be happy with some mediocre boyfriend and pathetic life.”</i><br><br>NO! <br>I'm afraid my brain refuses to read this!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396823702ra/9191437.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

<div id="review_1074353902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1074353902" />
    <a title="Bj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27341466-bj"><img alt="Bj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396449537p2/27341466.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1074353902?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bj" href="/user/show/27341466-bj">Bj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=mafia-cartel-romance">mafia-cartel-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27341466-bj?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074353902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1487642389236576015">5 "I'll Do Anything To Protect You--Even Make You Think I'm the Devil" Stars! <br/><br/>Wow, this book was amazing! What a twisted journey! I loved that you would never be able to figure out what this story is about from the first few pages or book blurb. For me the more suspenseful and convoluted the story, the better! So please don't be quick to make judgments. That's the point. This story is told from the heroine's POV, who is in the dark about who she really is and what she is really doing at Eagle El</span>
  <span id="freeText1487642389236576015" style="display:none">5 "I'll Do Anything To Protect You--Even Make You Think I'm the Devil" Stars! <br /><br />Wow, this book was amazing! What a twisted journey! I loved that you would never be able to figure out what this story is about from the first few pages or book blurb. For me the more suspenseful and convoluted the story, the better! So please don't be quick to make judgments. That's the point. This story is told from the heroine's POV, who is in the dark about who she really is and what she is really doing at Eagle Elite College. The beauty and creativeness of this book is how the story unfolds, and Rachel Van Dyken is a master, slowly revealing little clues along the way. In fact, even at the end of this book, you get the sense that there are still secrets that have yet to be unraveled, including who the heroine's true love match is. Yes, that's right, this series sports one of my favorite romance tropes: a love triangle! I can't wait to read book 2, Elect to see how this new adult gem continues to evolve!<br /><br />Trace Rooks lost her parents at a young age. Raised by her grandparents, who move to a farm in Wyoming to raise her, she has led a fairly wholesome life. Then she fulfills her grandmother's dying wish, when she wins and accepts the annual Eagle Elite College Scholarship to attend the prestigious university. Attending Elite, is usually an opportunity that is reserved for the extremely wealthy and future leaders of the country, so Trace believes it's a once in a lifetime opportunity for someone like her. <br /><br />As soon as she arrives, however, she realizes just what a different world Elite is. Almost immediately she meets mean students who make it their mission to make her question whether she belongs. Perhaps the worst of the them all is Nixon Abandonato, the class president. Everyone seems to cower at his command, even his ever present companion, and fellow Elect member, Chase, who seems to alternate between following Nixon's lead with his taunts and then challenging Nixon by showing genuine interest and concern for Trace. <br /><br />It doesn't take long for Nixon, however, to begin showing his own interest to Trace; and as his attention seems to alternate between protecting her and then acting like the devil; Trace realizes that she can't deny the inexplainable attraction that she too has to Nixon. It's not logical, but it is undeniable, and she is helpless to resist Nixon. <br /><br />But the Elect is hiding secrets, and their number one priority is protecting Trace, even if they have to hurt her in the process. Can there possibly be a HEA in the cards for Trace? Moreover, when the truths begin to be told, danger becomes even more omnipresent. Will Trace even manage to stay safe? <br /><br />All in all, this was a an amazing start to a promising new adult suspense-filled series, which also has a bit of a young adult feel. In that regard, please note that while there is tons of romantic tension, including the beginnings of a love triangle, this read is fairly tame from a love scenes perspective. The action and guessing as to where this series is going, however, both from a romantic and suspense perspective, will keep you joyfully entertained and clamoring for more! <br /><br />Source: Review copy provided by the publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1487642389236576015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17709172260278183684">HOLY HELL GUYS!! Rachel has done it again!! <br/><br/>I literally bought this book minutes after it went live on Amazon, i jumped up and seriously did a little happy dance (okay okay a major big happy dance!) I had been waiting and waiting for this and after all the little snippets Miss van Dyken had been posting for us lately i was dying to read it all together!<br/><br/>Well she definitely did not let us down (as if she could).<br/><br/>Without giving away too much i was at first like wow! that was so cruel, so nasty, what</span>
  <span id="freeText17709172260278183684" style="display:none">HOLY HELL GUYS!! Rachel has done it again!! <br /><br />I literally bought this book minutes after it went live on Amazon, i jumped up and seriously did a little happy dance (okay okay a major big happy dance!) I had been waiting and waiting for this and after all the little snippets Miss van Dyken had been posting for us lately i was dying to read it all together!<br /><br />Well she definitely did not let us down (as if she could).<br /><br />Without giving away too much i was at first like wow! that was so cruel, so nasty, what is she doing? but as the story progressed you could see that it all needed to be there.<br /><br />I loved every single character in this book..even the baddie cause if you don't love to hate the baddie in a book well then the author just hasn't done their job!<br />Trace- really liked her, gullible, sweet, naive,emotional,wise---real.<br />Monroe- everyone needs a friend like her!<br />Tex- too cute..definitely sweetheart material there<br />Phoenix-what can i say!<br />Chase-How how i love thee right from the beginning!<br />Nixon- Nixon,Nixon,Nixon-Poor guy, i can see why a lot of readers are not gonna like him but deep down if you really look beneath the surface you will see the true Nixon..this guy has got a lot of responsibility and sometimes you have to be a dick to save the ones you love!<br /><br />This is something different for Rachel but damn this girl is versatile..i think she could write anything and conquer any genre. Most definitely one of my favorite authors i seriously think i have a girl crush on her! lol<br /><br />A very solid 5 stars just because goodreads wont let me go over that!<br /><br />This book needs to be read by everyone! Well done Rachel, Well done!<br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16884018-the-hopeless-romantics-book-blog?shelf=arc-received-for-honest-review">arc-received-for-honest-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16884018-the-hopeless-romantics-book-blog?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1340510389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15042104366406595315">Facebook: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.facebook.com/TheHopelessRomanticsBookBlog'>https://www.facebook.com/TheHopelessR...</a><br/>TSU: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.tsu.co/HopelessRomantics'>http://www.tsu.co/HopelessRomantics</a><br/>Blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://thehopelessromanticsbookblog.blogspot.co.uk'>http://thehopelessromanticsbookblog.b...</a><br/><br/>I know I'm a little late to the party with this book. It had been on my kindle for a while and I finally got the chance to read it this weekend and now that I've finished it, I'm thinking why the hell did I leave it so long? From the moment I began reading this story I was hooked. <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>" Everything you've ever known..........is about to change." </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Tracey ha</span>
  <span id="freeText15042104366406595315" style="display:none">Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/TheHopelessRomanticsBookBlog">https://www.facebook.com/TheHopelessR...</a><br />TSU: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.tsu.co/HopelessRomantics">http://www.tsu.co/HopelessRomantics</a><br />Blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thehopelessromanticsbookblog.blogspot.co.uk">http://thehopelessromanticsbookblog.b...</a><br /><br />I know I'm a little late to the party with this book. It had been on my kindle for a while and I finally got the chance to read it this weekend and now that I've finished it, I'm thinking why the hell did I leave it so long? From the moment I began reading this story I was hooked. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>" Everything you've ever known..........is about to change." </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Tracey had won a place at an exclusive private school so the story began just as she was starting the move that would change her life, hopefully for the better. I instantly liked Tracey and I quickly became invested in her story. Following the death of her parents, Tracey had been living with her grandparents on their farm. She had been living a simple and sheltered life and was brought up to be kind, caring and loving. Tracey really didn't have a bad bone in her body. Moving to the prestigious boarding school, she had high hopes for her future. Unfortunately, she very quickly discovered that the school was not at all what she had imagined it to be. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>When I'd entered the lottery to go to this school, all I could think about was how I would be practically set for life. Now it seemed like I'd stepped into an action movie where the star had more power than the president of the United States.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Because I hardly ever read the synopsis of a book, I had no idea what I was in for so the minute things began to happen, my brain was working overtime trying to make sense of what I was reading. I was just as confused as Tracey so it was easy for me to put myself in her shoes and understand how she was feeling. As soon as Tracey met Nixon, things started to get weird and it continued that way until Tracey finally found out what was going on. Tracey showed a lot of courage during her first days at the school. I think I would have run away as soon as I got the chance! LOL. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Know that you make your own choices. You create your own destiny. And baby, I have the keys so either play by my rules, or don't. The choice is yours." </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Nixon was extremely good looking, but with his good looks also came a very confusing personality. One minute he was being an arse, treating Tracey so cruelly and the next minute he was being so caring and thoughtful towards her and promising to protect her no matter what. I didn't get why Nixon was acting the way he was with someone that he had only just met. I was completely baffled by his actions and Tracey was too. There was obviously some kind of connection between them and I couldn't put my kindle down until I had found out what it was. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"At least I can say I'd freaking bleed for you, if that's what it takes." <br />"Takes?" <br />"To keep you safe."<br />"So you'd die for me?" <br />"Don't you get it? I'd give my life for yours." </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />"Elite" was a fantastic start to a series. My only regret is that it took me so long to read it, but I will look on the bright side because I have a whole lot of books to catch up with now, which is what I am going to do as soon as I finish this review. "Elect" is already on my kindle waiting for me. If you looking for a new series to start that is full of suspense, intrigue and romance, I highly recommend giving this series a try. I am certain that you won't regret it. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I need you like I need my heart to pump blood through my body, like I need air to breathe, like we need gravity. Hell, Trace you are my gravity."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />"Elite (Eagle Elite #1)" gets ❤️❤️❤️❤️.5 from me! <br /></span>

<div id="review_1425132053" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425132053" />
    <a title="Zakirrah BookBlogger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15894726-zakirrah-bookblogger"><img alt="Zakirrah BookBlogger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396291066p2/15894726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425132053?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zakirrah BookBlogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zakirrah BookBlogger" href="/user/show/15894726-zakirrah-bookblogger">Zakirrah BookBlogger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15894726-zakirrah-bookblogger?shelf=arc-or-netgalley">arc-or-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425132053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8383674735528599404"><b>4 Elite Stars!! </b><br/><br/>Okay I am kicking myself for not reading this sooner! A friend of mine had been telling me to read it for a while and I blew it off, just not really giving it much thought and then I realised that I requested this book from NetGalley ages ago and never got round to it. I decided to finally put me foot down and get reading. I remember starting a few pages but I was in a book funk and gave up to try again at a later time. Right now I have my reading mojo back and I was totally read</span>
  <span id="freeText8383674735528599404" style="display:none"><b>4 Elite Stars!! </b><br /><br />Okay I am kicking myself for not reading this sooner! A friend of mine had been telling me to read it for a while and I blew it off, just not really giving it much thought and then I realised that I requested this book from NetGalley ages ago and never got round to it. I decided to finally put me foot down and get reading. I remember starting a few pages but I was in a book funk and gave up to try again at a later time. Right now I have my reading mojo back and I was totally ready for it. I actually really enjoyed it and will definitely be reading on.<br /><br />This is book 1 of Eagle Elite series and its got the whole mafia/criminal family thing going on which I had no idea about. My preconceived idea of this book was that it was some sort of spy/agent book? A school to train people in powers? Okay I can feel you all thinking what the hell? ..I don't even know what to say *shrugs* I guess I should stop assuming things.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Maybe the world isn't as shiny and fun as you once thought. People are mean. Humanity is a cruel joke, Trace. I'm just trying to prevent them from getting the last laugh." </b>
</i><br /><br />So the book, lets get back to the book. Trace is starting Eagle Elite College which is basically a college for the rich kids or those that will make the next presidents and so on. Trace is nothing like these people and the only reason she is here is because she won some sort of lottery that the college holds so one lucky winner gets to attend the college with all the rich people and so on.Trace is so out of her depth and it only gets worse when she meets Nixon and his crew who basically own the school and create all the rules. From then on things don't exactly go smoothly.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“—Nope. You’ve already broken a rule. I’m speaking, New Girl.” Chase smirked. “Geez, Nixon, this one’s going to be hard to break in.”<br />“They always are,” Nixon replied, lifting my chin with his hand. “But I think I’ll enjoy this one.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Nixon, oh Nixon at the start I was like what the hell? Why are you so mean! But with all assholes you end up loving them in the end. Well actually is went more like me hating him to liking him to feeling lost and losing interest in him and just not knowing how I feel. I liked him as a bad boy or more of the guy in charge. On another note I got this feeling of a love triangle which I thought or was hoping didn't exist but now I'm a little miffed and seriously don't want the next book to be a full n love triangle because they usually really irritate me and someone always gets hurt and i start hating the girl for loving two men. Like please woman, stop being greedy! <br /><br />Okay I'm going to quit ranting and get onto book 2, lets hope all goes well and it only gets better since I have heard a lot of people love this series. I want to be one of those people! ;) <br /><br /><i>*Arc provided by NetGalley for an honest review*<br />Blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://zakirrahsbookblog.blogspot.co.uk/">http://zakirrahsbookblog.blogspot.co.uk/</a><br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/ZakirrahsBookBlog">https://www.facebook.com/ZakirrahsBoo...</a><br />Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/ZBookBlog">https://twitter.com/ZBookBlog</a><br /></i></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jlSHs3IYs84ZYtCZ9c6d0MVGQSLxePB7WsuKtmyj4n0jpLH65oOu6okewuwjqvnjej745yZXF/lnEFqzfFtc2w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F/wsj9/YQZFbYOL1s6TDFDgvHOI7L9AQMS2OgosALlG6DBrGS0Nctcsc8IBlwKcnh1elJ+wAN5IM9l6Hm/iQ9w==')})
  }
